The Waste/CE Market Analysis  \n1.1 Facts & Figures  Waste Generation and \nComposition  \nIn 2018, Peru produced 7.3 million tons of Municipal \nWaste, or 0.63 kilograms per person per day. 57.7% was \norganic waste; 18.3% recyclables such as plastic, \naluminum and paper; and  24.1% was residual wasteix. Of \nthe 20,000 tons of garbage produced daily, a third is \ngenerated in Lima. According to official data, only 1% \nof the municipal waste is being valorized; 4% of the dry \nrecyclable waste and 1% of organicsx. Information is \nscarce and mostly limited to the formal sector, even \nthough the informal sector recycles more than the formal \nsector . \nAdditionally, 28.9 million tons of non -Municipal Waste \nper year is generated, 59.5% of which comes from \nindustry, 16.1% from agriculture and 9.5% from mining \n(National Environmental Action Plan 2011 -2021 \nPLA...",

  "snippet_or_summary": "JavaScript is disabled on your browser.\n      Please enable JavaScript to use all the features on this page.\nSkip to main content\nSkip to article\nScienceDirect\nJournals & Books\nHelp\nSearch\nMy account\nSign in\nView\nPDF\nDownload full issue\nSearch ScienceDirect\nCity and Environment Interactions\nVolume 20\n,\nDecember 2023\n, 100112\nSolid waste management and urban environmental quality of public space in Chiclayo, Peru\nAuthor links open overlay panel\nCarlos\nArteaga\n,\nJhon\nSilva\n,\nCristian\nYarasca-Aybar\nShow more\nAdd to Mendeley\nShare\nCite\nhttps://doi.org/10.1016/j.cacint.2023.100112\nGet rights and content\nUnder a Creative Commons\nlicense\nOpen access\nAbstract\nSolid Waste Management (SWM) through planning and technical coordination is essential for the sustainable development of cities in terms of social, physical, territorial, and legal-political aspects. During the last 20\u00a0years, Chiclayo has been the most polluted city in northern Peru owing to its poor municipal solid waste (MSW) management. This study aims to determine the level of urban impact generated by SWM on the configuration of public spaces in the districts of Jos\u00e9 Leonardo Ortiz, La Victoria, and Chiclayo (homonymous district). Management actors were identified with a territorial diagnosis for methodological analysis to obtain efficiency indices. The scope of management in the last ten years was determined using the Fisher-Davies method and Leopold diagrams, and the results obtained were compared with the population's perception. The discussion of the results determined that SWM has a negative level of urban environmental impact on the configuration of public spaces. These have a very negative impact on the biotic and abiotic factors of the urban landscape as well as on sociocultural factors. This study provides evidence of the implications of city governance on territorial sustainability. This will allow for the development of thematic frameworks that address urban, environmental, socioeconomic, and technologi...",

During the last 20\u00a0years, Chiclayo has been the most polluted city in northern Peru owing to its poor municipal solid waste (MSW) management. This study aims to determine the level of urban impact generated by SWM on the configuration of public spaces in the districts of Jos\u00e9 Leonardo Ortiz, La Victoria, and Chiclayo (homonymous district). Management actors were identified with a territorial diagnosis for methodological analysis to obtain efficiency indices. The scope of management in the last ten years was determined using the Fisher-Davies method and Leopold diagrams, and the results obtained were compared with the population's perception. The discussion of the results determined that SWM has a negative level of urban environmental impact on the configuration of public spaces. These have a very negative impact on the biotic and abiotic factors of the urban landscape as well as on sociocultural factors. This study provides evidence of the implications of city governance on territorial sustainability. This will allow for the development of thematic frameworks that address urban, environmental, socioeconomic, and technologi...",

During the last 20\u00a0years, Chiclayo has been the most polluted city in northern Peru owing to its poor municipal solid waste (MSW) management. This study aims to determine the level of urban impact generated by SWM on the configuration of public spaces in the districts of Jos\u00e9 Leonardo Ortiz, La Victoria, and Chiclayo (homonymous district). Management actors were identified with a territorial diagnosis for methodological analysis to obtain efficiency indices. The scope of management in the last ten years was determined using the Fisher-Davies method and Leopold diagrams, and the results obtained were compared with the population's perception. The discussion of the results determined that SWM has a negative level of urban environmental impact on the configuration of public spaces. These have a very negative impact on the biotic and abiotic factors of the urban landscape as well as on sociocultural factors. This study provides evidence of the implications of city governance on territorial sustainability. This will allow for the development of thematic frameworks that address urban, environmental, socioeconomic, and technologi...",

This study provides evidence of the implications of city governance on territorial sustainability. Management actors were identified with a territorial diagnosis for methodological analysis to obtain efficiency indices. The scope of management in the last ten years was determined using the Fisher-Davies method and Leopold diagrams, and the results obtained were compared with the population's perception. The discussion of the results determined that SWM has a negative level of urban environmental impact on the configuration of public spaces. These have a very negative impact on the biotic and abiotic factors of the urban landscape as well as on sociocultural factors. This study provides evidence of the implications of city governance on territorial sustainability. This will allow for the development of thematic frameworks that address urban, environmental, socioeconomic, and technologi...",

During the last 20\u00a0years, Chiclayo has been the most polluted city in northern Peru owing to its poor municipal solid waste (MSW) management. This study aims to determine the level of urban impact generated by SWM on the configuration of public spaces in the districts of Jos\u00e9 Leonardo Ortiz, La Victoria, and Chiclayo (homonymous district). Management actors were identified with a territorial diagnosis for methodological analysis to obtain efficiency indices. The discussion of the results determined that SWM has a negative level of urban environmental impact on the configuration of public spaces. These have a very negative impact on the biotic and abiotic factors of the urban landscape as well as on sociocultural factors. This study provides evidence of the implications of city governance on territorial sustainability. This will allow for the development of thematic frameworks that address urban, environmental, socioeconomic, and technologi...",

This study aims to determine the level of urban impact generated by SWM on the configuration of public spaces in the districts of Jos\u00e9 Leonardo Ortiz, La Victoria, and Chiclayo (homonymous district). Management actors were identified with a territorial diagnosis for methodological analysis to obtain efficiency indices. The scope of management in the last ten years was determined using the Fisher-Davies method and Leopold diagrams, and the results obtained were compared with the population's perception. The discussion of the results determined that SWM has a negative level of urban environmental impact on the configuration of public spaces. These have a very negative impact on the biotic and abiotic factors of the urban landscape as well as on sociocultural factors. This study provides evidence of the implications of city governance on territorial sustainability. This will allow for the development of thematic frameworks that address urban, environmental, socioeconomic, and technologi...",

During the last 20\u00a0years, Chiclayo has been the most polluted city in northern Peru owing to its poor municipal solid waste (MSW) management. This study aims to determine the level of urban impact generated by SWM on the configuration of public spaces in the districts of Jos\u00e9 Leonardo Ortiz, La Victoria, and Chiclayo (homonymous district). Management actors were identified with a territorial diagnosis for methodological analysis to obtain efficiency indices. The scope of management in the last ten years was determined using the Fisher-Davies method and Leopold diagrams, and the results obtained were compared with the population's perception. The discussion of the results determined that SWM has a negative level of urban environmental impact on the configuration of public spaces. These have a very negative impact on the biotic and abiotic factors of the urban landscape as well as on sociocultural factors. This study provides evidence of the implications of city governance on territorial sustainability. This will allow for the development of thematic frameworks that address urban, environmental, socioeconomic, and technologi...",

This study aims to determine the level of urban impact generated by SWM on the configuration of public spaces in the districts of Jos\u00e9 Leonardo Ortiz, La Victoria, and Chiclayo (homonymous district). Management actors were identified with a territorial diagnosis for methodological analysis to obtain efficiency indices. The scope of management in the last ten years was determined using the Fisher-Davies method and Leopold diagrams, and the results obtained were compared with the population's perception. The discussion of the results determined that SWM has a negative level of urban environmental impact on the configuration of public spaces. These have a very negative impact on the biotic and abiotic factors of the urban landscape as well as on sociocultural factors. This study provides evidence of the implications of city governance on territorial sustainability. This will allow for the development of thematic frameworks that address urban, environmental, socioeconomic, and technologi...",

  "snippet_or_summary": "JavaScript is disabled on your browser.\n      Please enable JavaScript to use all the features on this page.\nSkip to main content\nSkip to article\nScienceDirect\nJournals & Books\nHelp\nSearch\nMy account\nSign in\nView\nPDF\nDownload full issue\nSearch ScienceDirect\nCity and Environment Interactions\nVolume 20\n,\nDecember 2023\n, 100112\nSolid waste management and urban environmental quality of public space in Chiclayo, Peru\nAuthor links open overlay panel\nCarlos\nArteaga\n,\nJhon\nSilva\n,\nCristian\nYarasca-Aybar\nShow more\nAdd to Mendeley\nShare\nCite\nhttps://doi.org/10.1016/j.cacint.2023.100112\nGet rights and content\nUnder a Creative Commons\nlicense\nOpen access\nAbstract\nSolid Waste Management (SWM) through planning and technical coordination is essential for the sustainable development of cities in terms of social, physical, territorial, and legal-political aspects. During the last 20\u00a0years, Chiclayo has been the most polluted city in northern Peru owing to its poor municipal solid waste (MSW) management. This study aims to determine the level of urban impact generated by SWM on the configuration of public spaces in the districts of Jos\u00e9 Leonardo Ortiz, La Victoria, and Chiclayo (homonymous district). Management actors were identified with a territorial diagnosis for methodological analysis to obtain efficiency indices. The scope of management in the last ten years was determined using the Fisher-Davies method and Leopold diagrams, and the results obtained were compared with the population's perception. The discussion of the results determined that SWM has a negative level of urban environmental impact on the configuration of public spaces. These have a very negative impact on the biotic and abiotic factors of the urban landscape as well as on sociocultural factors. This study provides evidence of the implications of city governance on territorial sustainability. This will allow for the development of thematic frameworks that address urban, environmental, socioeconomic, and technologi...",

  "title": "Solid waste management and urban environmental quality of public space in Chiclayo, Peru - ScienceDirect",
  "snippet_or_summary": "JavaScript is disabled on your browser.\n      Please enable JavaScript to use all the features on this page.\nSkip to main content\nSkip to article\nScienceDirect\nJournals & Books\nHelp\nSearch\nMy account\nSign in\nView\nPDF\nDownload full issue\nSearch ScienceDirect\nCity and Environment Interactions\nVolume 20\n,\nDecember 2023\n, 100112\nSolid waste management and urban environmental quality of public space in Chiclayo, Peru\nAuthor links open overlay panel\nCarlos\nArteaga\n,\nJhon\nSilva\n,\nCristian\nYarasca-Aybar\nShow more\nAdd to Mendeley\nShare\nCite\nhttps://doi.org/10.1016/j.cacint.2023.100112\nGet rights and content\nUnder a Creative Commons\nlicense\nOpen access\nAbstract\nSolid Waste Management (SWM) through planning and technical coordination is essential for the sustainable development of cities in terms of social, physical, territorial, and legal-political aspects. During the last 20\u00a0years, Chiclayo has been the most polluted city in northern Peru owing to its poor municipal solid waste (MSW) management. This study aims to determine the level of urban impact generated by SWM on the configuration of public spaces in the districts of Jos\u00e9 Leonardo Ortiz, La Victoria, and Chiclayo (homonymous district). Management actors were identified with a territorial diagnosis for methodological analysis to obtain efficiency indices. The scope of management in the last ten years was determined using the Fisher-Davies method and Leopold diagrams, and the results obtained were compared with the population's perception. The discussion of the results determined that SWM has a negative level of urban environmental impact on the configuration of public spaces. These have a very negative impact on the biotic and abiotic factors of the urban landscape as well as on sociocultural factors. This study provides evidence of the implications of city governance on territorial sustainability. This will allow for the development of thematic frameworks that address urban, environmental, socioeconomic, and technologi...",

The two year programme (2013 to 2015) is supported by the Nordic Working Group for Global Climate Negotiations (NOAK) and the Nordic Environment Finance Corporation (NEFCO). It is implemented and coordinated by the Peruvian Ministry of Environment (MINAM). The \u2018Programme for supporting upscaled mitigation action in Peru\u2019s waste sector under the Nordic Partnership Initiative\u2019 aims at exploring possibilities to lower GHG emissions in Peru\u2019s solid waste sector and demonstrating in practice how international climate finance can be matched with upscaled host country mitigation action. It will look at the potential of existing waste management options for decreasing emissions as well as eliminating relevant technical financial and other barriers to more sustainable waste management practices and also address the necessary framework for increased private sector engagement. The activities of the programme include improvement of the solid waste data base an extensive stakeholder process a GEI inventory for the sector improvements to the country\u2019s solid waste monitoring system the development of a sector mitigation strategy and the development of a detailed nationally appropriate mitigation action (NAMA) option including measuring reporting and verification (MRV) and financing options among other things. It shall put special emphasis on exploring opportunities to utilise market-based mechanisms and a results-based approach for the provision of future support. Furthermore it aims at sharing valuable lessons on practical issues related to new climate finance and carbon market mechanisms as well as to implementing mitigation strategies in the waste sector. An international consortium of consultants lead by NIRAS (Denmark) is supporting MINAM in...",

The Waste/CE Market Analysis 1.1 Facts & Figures Waste Generation and Composition In 2018, Peru produced 7.3 million tons of Municipal Waste, or 0.63 kilograms per person per day. 57.7% was organic waste; 18.3% recyclables such as plastic, aluminum and paper; and 24.1% was residual wasteix. Of the 20,000 tons of garbage produced daily, a third is generated in Lima. According to official data, only 1% of the municipal waste is being valorized; 4% of the dry recyclable waste and 1% of organicsx.
